  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f2362bc9-0c3f-46e5-bb74-f074260b1638'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer9979778577950635367">Halt's Peril (Ranger's Apprentice #9), John Flanagan<br/><br/>Halt's Peril is the ninth book in the international best-selling Ranger's Apprentice series by John Flanagan. It was released on 2 November 2009 in Australia.<br/><br/>Halt and Will (both legendary Rangers) and the knight Horace discover that Tennyson, the leader of the Outsiders cult, and his followers have fled to Picta, a country to the north of Araluen. <br/><br/>They discover where the Outsiders went from a smuggler named Black O'Malley. The three follow thei</span>
  <span id="freeText9979778577950635367" style="display:none">Halt's Peril (Ranger's Apprentice #9), John Flanagan<br /><br />Halt's Peril is the ninth book in the international best-selling Ranger's Apprentice series by John Flanagan. It was released on 2 November 2009 in Australia.<br /><br />Halt and Will (both legendary Rangers) and the knight Horace discover that Tennyson, the leader of the Outsiders cult, and his followers have fled to Picta, a country to the north of Araluen. <br /><br />They discover where the Outsiders went from a smuggler named Black O'Malley. The three follow their trail and discover that Tennyson is heading toward Araluen. <br /><br />Tennyson's plan is to travel to an outlying Araluen village where he has already established influence to reinvigorate his movement. <br /><br />Will and his companions are unaware of this, however, and continue to follow Tennyson through Picta, discovering and foiling some Pictan raiders on the way. <br /><br />As the three catch up to Tennyson they engage with the remaining two of his hired assassins. Halt and Will successfully kill one, but the other injures Halt and escapes.<br /><br />After a while, the wound is discovered to be poisoned by a hallucinogen which is slowly killing Halt. In desperation Will decides to seek the healer Malcolm and brings him to help. Malcolm explains that the poison has two possible sources with conflicting cures. <br /><br />Administering the wrong cure will kill Halt. Will discovers the remaining assassin and forces the nature of the poison from him by cutting him with his own arrow. The assassin is killed when he later attempts to escape.<br /><br />With Halt cured, the three along with Malcolm continue to trail Tennyson. Will and his companions discover Tennyson in catacombs near a village where he is preaching to the followers of his religion. Halt successfully discredits him with Malcolm's help. <br /><br />In the chaos that follows, the cave system collapses on top of Tennyson and the Outsiders and all their gold. Halt, Will and Horace and Malcolm escape, and escort Malcom back to his home in Grimsdell Wood. Once there, Will's friend Trobar gives Will a puppy, Ebony, the daughter of the dog Shadow which Will gave to Trobar in The Siege of Macindaw. <br /><br />After separating from Malcolm, the trio head home, with Will and Halt going to Redmont and reuniting with Pauline and Alyss while Horace heads to Castle Araluen.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز شانزدهم ماه سپتامبر سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: هالت در خطر مرگ؛ نویسنده: جان فلنگن؛ مترجم: مسعود ملک‌یاری؛ ویراستار: مرجان مهدی‌پور؛ تهران: افق‏‫، 1396؛ در 459ص؛ شابک 9786003533790؛ فروست سری جنگاوران کتاب نهم؛ ‬‬چاپ دوم 1397؛ موضوع داستانهای نوجوانان از نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 21م<br /><br />هالت و ویل در تعقیب باقی‌مانده‌ ی فرقه‌ ی بیگانگان در جنگل با دو مبارز خطرناک روبرو می‌شوند و تیری زهرآگین هالت را زخمی می‌کند. اکنون استاد ویل در بستر مرگ افتاده و تنها یک نفر می‌تواند جان او را نجات دهد.؛ رنجر جوان وقت زیادی ندارد و باید از جاده‌ های مخوف و جنگل پرخطر بگذرد تا تنها امیدش مالکالام جادوگر را پیدا کند. کتاب «هالت در خطر مرگ- جنگاوران جوان 9» نهمین جلد از مجموعه‌ ی دوازده جلدی جنگاوران جوان است.؛ این مجموعه به عنوان پرفروش‌ترین کتاب‌ها به انتخاب نیویورک‌تایمز برگزیده شده‌ اند.؛ تاکنون دوازده جلد از این مجموعه‌ منتشر شده است؛ نشر افق با خرید حق انتشار آنها در ایران،‌ تاکنون نه جلد را منتشر کرده، و دو جلد دیگر نیز در دست انتشار است<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 09/05/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="9979778577950635367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6632442766408199283">I just love everything Flanagan has done with this series. I am so disappointed only by the fact that I only have 1 book left + the lost stories. I have already put book one of his outcast series on hold for my kindle and am deperately waiting for it to come in.<br/><br/>This series has a perfect blend of action, plot development, character development, dialouge and depth of relationships....basically everything one could want in a fantasy series. In this edition Halt, Will & Horace pick up the chase that</span>
  <span id="freeText6632442766408199283" style="display:none">I just love everything Flanagan has done with this series. I am so disappointed only by the fact that I only have 1 book left + the lost stories. I have already put book one of his outcast series on hold for my kindle and am deperately waiting for it to come in.<br /><br />This series has a perfect blend of action, plot development, character development, dialouge and depth of relationships....basically everything one could want in a fantasy series. In this edition Halt, Will &amp; Horace pick up the chase that was left off in the previous book. Now that they have hindered the spread of the devious outsiders cult that plauged Clomnell...they persue them back into Arulean where the tattered remains of the cult seek to reestablish their control of the masses. The dock side encounters were pretty eventful as well as humerous. Their persuit of the enemy cult leader led to the main predicament in this book "Halt's Peril". And as halt gets caught into a battle for life and death, Will goes and brings back an old friend from books 5 &amp; 6 Malcolm. it was nice getting aquainted with him, and who knows a side series about him could prove interesting. It would be fun to see how a back water healer has knowledge of some of the worlds most secret and notorious dangers. The deepening friendship between the 3 amigos, has been fun to watch them grow as individuals as well as collectively in their relationships with one another. Horace has gone from a simply faithful side kick, to a fearsome partner and offers many humerous antecdotes to give some levity to the story.<br /><br />My only disappointment again is that it seems as with all good things this series to must someday end!</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6879652-mara?shelf=kingdom-adventure">kingdom-adventure</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231217933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10519442679728082536">I have put off writing this review as long as I can. No, I haven't put it off because I have such dreadful things to say about it; I put it off so that I may think of what to say about it. Unfortunately, there really isn't anything in Halt's Peril to excite particular interest in a positive or negative way.<br/><br/>It is a good installment, and fairly suspensful, though its ending is easy to guess. Mr. Flanagan isn't an Author who allows permanent evil to befall main characters. Like all of the books, hi</span>
  <span id="freeText10519442679728082536" style="display:none">I have put off writing this review as long as I can. No, I haven't put it off because I have such dreadful things to say about it; I put it off so that I may think of what to say about it. Unfortunately, there really isn't anything in Halt's Peril to excite particular interest in a positive or negative way.<br /><br />It is a good installment, and fairly suspensful, though its ending is easy to guess. Mr. Flanagan isn't an Author who allows permanent evil to befall main characters. Like all of the books, his dialogue is funny, but movie-ish, though I must say that some of the interactions between the characters in this volume are particularly funny. I am also pleased to report that Flanagan does not try to tackle any battles, but a few minor skirmishes. He can do that, and I must admit that his avoidance of trying to write a real battle improves the books considerably.<br /><br />Still, I wish he wasn't writing any more books in the Ranger's Apprentice series. Four was a perfect number; six was really pushing it. But ten?! (And I hear rumors that there is to be an 11th.) Even the best of serieses need to end, otherwise they become dull and slightly irksome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10519442679728082536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4130591629619862129">Will, Horace, and Halt travel from Hibernia to Picta to Araluen, chasing down a band of murderous wolves in sheep's clothing. They must destroy this treacherous cult once and for all, but contending with ice-cold assassins (Sicilian-style) nearly costs them everything, as the title suggests. (Chillingly vivid portrayals of Genovesan assassins at work).<br/><br/>Another fast-paced and somewhat heartwarming tale of courage, strategy, and friendship. It was nice to see some old friends from a few prior books</span>
  <span id="freeText4130591629619862129" style="display:none">Will, Horace, and Halt travel from Hibernia to Picta to Araluen, chasing down a band of murderous wolves in sheep's clothing. They must destroy this treacherous cult once and for all, but contending with ice-cold assassins (Sicilian-style) nearly costs them everything, as the title suggests. (Chillingly vivid portrayals of Genovesan assassins at work).<br /><br />Another fast-paced and somewhat heartwarming tale of courage, strategy, and friendship. It was nice to see some old friends from a few prior books — great secondary characters. I felt the scenes where Halt was in deadly peril were detailed and credible. However, some scenes were hard to believe, like the amazing feats of archery aboard the Swallow. I chuckled at the farmers, angry about their scattered herd. So true to life!<br /><br />This book picked up where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5201089.The_Kings_of_Clonmel__Ranger_s_Apprentice___8_" title="The Kings of Clonmel (Ranger's Apprentice, #8) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kings of Clonmel</a> left off. With the conclusion of this book, the two-book plot is nicely tied off with a bow.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7924474896613821783">I really did like this book. I feel as though the book never truly adds anything new to the table, plot wise. I have also seen reviews bashing the book for just that. However this wasn't a book intended to add anything new. It was intended to tie up the current story arc. Clearing the stage for the next act, if <br/>you will. Halt's Peril wasn't great at adding new elements into the mix of Ranger's Apprentice, but it stirs the pot of characters a little. Will and Alyss's relationship is hinted at in </span>
  <span id="freeText7924474896613821783" style="display:none">I really did like this book. I feel as though the book never truly adds anything new to the table, plot wise. I have also seen reviews bashing the book for just that. However this wasn't a book intended to add anything new. It was intended to tie up the current story arc. Clearing the stage for the next act, if <br />you will. Halt's Peril wasn't great at adding new elements into the mix of Ranger's Apprentice, but it stirs the pot of characters a little. Will and Alyss's relationship is hinted at in the last chapter, and it is revealed that Horace and Cassandra (or Evanlyn, if that's what you want to call her) are romantically connected. And Halt starts to realize that his age is catching up to him. All-in-all I'd say it is great at tying up the loose ends caused by previous books and hinting at things yet to come. I hope book 10 is as good as this one.</span>

<div id="review_1394781794" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394781794" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394781794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14264640070691638633"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> series is quickly becoming one of my all-time favourite series. It has everything I love in a series: fantastic characters, great storylines that never get repetitive, an impressive range of settings and it has always given me that wonderful feeling of needing <i>more</i>immediately after finishing. I never want the stories to end.<br/><br/>That being said, I didn't think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6348045.Halt_s_Peril__Ranger_s_Apprentice___9_' title='Halt's Peril (Ranger's Apprentice, #9) by John Flanagan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Halt's Peril</a> was the best book of the series so far. I enjoyed seeing the story of the last book get wrapped </span>
  <span id="freeText14264640070691638633" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />The <i>Ranger's Apprentice</i> series is quickly becoming one of my all-time favourite series. It has everything I love in a series: fantastic characters, great storylines that never get repetitive, an impressive range of settings and it has always given me that wonderful feeling of needing <i>more</i>immediately after finishing. I never want the stories to end.<br /><br />That being said, I didn't think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6348045.Halt_s_Peril__Ranger_s_Apprentice___9_" title="Halt's Peril (Ranger's Apprentice, #9) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">Halt's Peril</a> was the best book of the series so far. I enjoyed seeing the story of the last book get wrapped up, but I especially loved that it wasn't easy. I love that some of the character got hurt - well, not <i>loved</i> it exactly. I'm not a masochist! But I enjoyed that we got to see Halt fail a little bit. In real life, our trio obviously wouldn't be perfect and they didn't pretend to be this time. They got hurt, they got sick, and they had to change their plans numerous times.<br /><br />Because of this though, we got a lot more character development rather then action. Again, this wasn't necessarily bad thing as we got to know the character a little better and got more of their hilarious, adorable moments together. It didn't get a little slow at times, which is why it took me a little longer to read then normal <br /><br />Overall, this book was still incredible. I love these three characters - Halt, Will and Horace - so very much. And it made me cry. Twice. I cannot wait to dive into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7592279.The_Emperor_of_Nihon_Ja__Ranger_s_Apprentice___10_" title="The Emperor of Nihon-Ja (Ranger's Apprentice, #10) by John Flanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor of Nihon-Ja</a> as it follows Horace - I think? - and he's easily my favourite character.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14264640070691638633" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_770776027" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770776027" />
    <a title="Keilani Ludlow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3361842-keilani-ludlow"><img alt="Keilani Ludlow" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770776027?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keilani Ludlow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keilani Ludlow" href="/user/show/3361842-keilani-ludlow">Keilani Ludlow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770776027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18166926716070693374">From this point forward in the series, I am just cutting and pasting my previous info with a separate paragraph at the bottom specific to this particular book in the series.<br/><br/>If you check out my other 4 stars, you'll see that there is some stiff competition and I don't hand it out lightly. If you are really into Brandon Sanderson, Robert Jordan, etc. you may find these a little bit light. However, as I stated above, they grow, and I really enjoy that they are totally enthralling but at the same ti</span>
  <span id="freeText18166926716070693374" style="display:none">From this point forward in the series, I am just cutting and pasting my previous info with a separate paragraph at the bottom specific to this particular book in the series.<br /><br />If you check out my other 4 stars, you'll see that there is some stiff competition and I don't hand it out lightly. If you are really into Brandon Sanderson, Robert Jordan, etc. you may find these a little bit light. However, as I stated above, they grow, and I really enjoy that they are totally enthralling but at the same time I can listen to them with my children in the car or hand the books to my sons when I'm done and not wince about anything in them - which can't be said for the authors mentioned above.<br /><br />Basically - Fantasy in the style that is almost old-fashioned in setting due to the lack of anything modern. Not a lot in the way of magic, in-fact nearly nothing. People in a medieval type setting and some occasional weird creatures, references to Gods and religions, and so on. <br /><br />The main characters are rangers and they could be compared to woods elves in many series, American Indians, even Daniel Boone and early settlers. They learn the skills to be unseen, to walk through a forest without leaving a path, to track others, they learn archery and knife skills, they serve as the King's eyes and ears and they solve problems. They are awesome! There are also knights, kings, bakers, diplomats, and so on. There are also a variety of countries and cultures which makes it more interesting because you don’t see the mix of social structure usually in old-fashioned type books.<br /><br />After the first book, the rest of the series pretty much develops the social structure, the characters and their relationships, and all as they go on adventures to support good and defeat evil! I admit it, as much as I love reading books involving complicated social questions and philosophies, I also love reading books that are clear cut in most ways. Here is the bad guy, now figure out how to take him out, and by the end they do take him out. No dithering, no years in court or excuses, it just gets done.<br /><br />All the books seem to be two part. Book 1 starts the adventure and book 2 completes it, though right at the end of book two they start the adventure that is covered in book 3. Book 4 tags on to 3 but is a separate adventure. Books 5-6 go together and jump ahead several years. The author then comes back to the main timeline in books 7 and then 8-9 take place after books 5-6. If you read 7 after 4, then 5-6 and then 8-9 onward it would be less confusing, but the author wrote them this way so maybe he had a reason. Because each book does refer back to events in previous books, the skip in timeline makes it a bit weird. I haven't read 10 yet (my son stole it from me) but I'll let you know where that fits when I get to it. <br /><br />Book 9 - The follow up and conclusion to book 9. Halt's life is on the line, the great deceiver has been temporarily defeated but still lives and proceeds with his violent and manipulative ways. A friend from the past and things learned from previous experiences are brought in to help. Very good story, well written. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18166926716070693374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119467746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119467746" />
    <a title="Library Lady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/138271-library-lady"><img alt="Library Lady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222454918p2/138271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119467746?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Library Lady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Library Lady" href="/user/show/138271-library-lady">Library Lady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780399252075" href="/book/show/7291741-halt-s-peril">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138271-library-lady?shelf=children-s-and-ya-fantasy-sci-fi">children-s-and-ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138271-library-lady?shelf=galley">galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138271-library-lady?shelf=my-50-in-2010">my-50-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119467746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer840256105419049871">While I did like this book, it wasn't as good as the others in the series. The bantering between Halt, Horace, and Will was great, and I loved the action sequences, but the plot seemed a little disjointed. Actually, in form and tone this book reminded me quite a lot of the third book in the series, which is the one that I remember the most clearly. (I think this is because it was that book that made me realize how much I loved the series since I was so worried and heart-sick over Will!)<br/><br/>I also li</span>
  <span id="freeText840256105419049871" style="display:none">While I did like this book, it wasn't as good as the others in the series. The bantering between Halt, Horace, and Will was great, and I loved the action sequences, but the plot seemed a little disjointed. Actually, in form and tone this book reminded me quite a lot of the third book in the series, which is the one that I remember the most clearly. (I think this is because it was that book that made me realize how much I loved the series since I was so worried and heart-sick over Will!)<br /><br />I also like the realization that Halt is getting older. I think Flanagan may be getting near the end of the series, now. Halt will have to retire soon and while it would be fun to see Will with a new apprentice, it just wouldn't be the same. I love Halt and would hate to continue the series without him. Having him in peril was very emotional, creating great dramatic tension.<br /><br />I can see why some would be irritated with the anti-religious bent of the eighth and ninth books, but I look at it as Flanagan really speaking to the power and awfulness of cults. During the Middle Ages there was a lot of religious fanaticism and superstition, and I think he's calling attention to that. Araluen is basically Medieval England, so for him to use such situations in his world makes sense to me.<br /><br />One more thing: while she was barely mentioned in the book, I still find myself annoyed by Will's relationship with Alys. I think she's fine as a character, but she doesn't seem right for Will to me. There just doesn't seem to be a strong bond between them, even after everything that happened in the fifth and sixth books. Maybe it's because the third book resonated with me so much, but I think Will has a stronger bond with Evanlyn. I'm hoping that the "triangle" such as it is, is explored more. Even though Flanagan doesn't write romance really well, I'd still like to see the attraction and connection between Will and Evanlyn settled. Every time Flanagan mentions Horace and Evanlyn I cringe a little, wondering if she still harbors feelings for Will and I would hate for Horace to be a second choice. All romance talk aside, the strength in these books is, and always has been, Flanagan's gift with action sequences and the strong bonds between men. I love reading those and I'm glad this book had a lot of that!</span>
  <a data-text-id="840256105419049871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2953217766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2953217766" />
    <a title="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor"><img alt="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567608261p2/95618407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2953217766?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smaug the Unmerciful Editor" href="/user/show/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor">Smaug the Unmerciful Editor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8823218-halt-s-peril">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor?shelf=unbelievably-dumb">unbelievably-dumb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/95618407-smaug-the-unmerciful-editor?shelf=moderately-clean">moderately-clean</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2953217766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3949967377168084784">To John Flanagan's credit: this book is amazingly 99% clean. I mean, how many of those do you find in the YA shelves? Pretty much none! So good for John for making a clean YA (even though his books are pretty goofy).<br/><br/>I can't really complain about the prose. What's there to say? It's fine. Not great, not bad. But the characters, OH the CHARACTERS! Another example of John's stereotypical brains-vs-brawn! All the big, burly warriors are the dull-witted thugs who LITERALLY say "I'll leave the thinkin</span>
  <span id="freeText3949967377168084784" style="display:none">To John Flanagan's credit: this book is amazingly 99% clean. I mean, how many of those do you find in the YA shelves? Pretty much none! So good for John for making a clean YA (even though his books are pretty goofy).<br /><br />I can't really complain about the prose. What's there to say? It's fine. Not great, not bad. But the characters, OH the CHARACTERS! Another example of John's stereotypical brains-vs-brawn! All the big, burly warriors are the dull-witted thugs who LITERALLY say "I'll leave the thinking to you, smart Rangers!" while the short people and all the girls (the girls who are deemed attractive, by the way, are all super tall, super smart, and super blonde) are smart as a whip, clever in their comebacks, and pretty much all-around flawless. I mean, <i>WHAT?</i><br /><br />And the story is pretty lacking, too. It's not so bad, when I think about it: things happen in an orderly fashion that makes sense, but the entire premise of the title. "Halt's Peril," is that Halt is in danger! But Halt's only in peril for the third quarter of the book, and that's it. Not the first half, not the last quarter! Just for that minuscule amount of time. Pretty disappointing. And the rest of the book is just a boring bar scene (where the Rangers once again prove their cleverness the Horace the Thug once again proves his walnut-sized cranium) and the chase after Tennyson, the obviously evil, cackling-behind-his-hand, greedy and physically unfit false prophet. What's the point? Who knows! They could have led a platoon of soldiers in there, seized Tennyson (who may or may not have a connection to aliens and a strange watch?), read the charges aloud to the crowd, and went on their way, but NO! <i>Yet again</i> the Rangers just <i>have</i> to show everyone how <i>smart</i> they are! I'm not gonna tell you HOW, 'cause then it'd be spoilers. But suffice to say it could have been done in a cheaper, faster and more effective manner.<br /><br />My unexpert verdict: it's pretty bad, but worth a read anyway because a) it's famous and b) it's clean, besides a few mild swear words here and there. Seriously, if it wasn't clean, it would be AWFUL. But John proves that something doesn't have to be dirty to be famous. Kudos to him for that, at least.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3949967377168084784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_722834276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722834276" />
    <a title="Caleb P" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23073159-caleb-p"><img alt="Caleb P" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722834276?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caleb P" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caleb P" href="/user/show/23073159-caleb-p">Caleb P</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722834276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15068691285909349692">Has someone really important to you ever been in a lot of trouble and you couldn't do any thing?   <span id="freeText15068691285909349692" style="display:none">Has someone really important to you ever been in a lot of trouble and you couldn't do any thing? In Rangers Apprentice Halt's Peril book 9 by John Flanagan: Halt, Will, and Horace(men fighting for the king) Halt is a quiet ranger who can move around without being seen using a cloak. Will is a new ranger who looks up to halt like a father and tries hard to please him. Horace is a broad shouldered knight who is a experienced sword fighter who looks to Halt and Will as family. They are chasing a group called the outsiders. They are a religious cult that may look good on the outside but really are attacking people.They chase them through mountains but are attacked by hired assassins called genovesians. One of the assassins scrape Halt the trios leader with a poison arrow. Halt starts to fall in and out of consciousness and is slowly dieing when Will comes up with an idea, to ride to Macindaw and find a old friend named Malcolm to save Halt. Will will get Malcolm to Halt in time or will Halt die before Will can reach him. I rate this book 5 stars because you are always interested in the book. You don't want to put the book down from beginning to end. the end and beginning are exciting the whole time making this book great the whole way through. For example, When Halt gets shot with the arrow you think its the end because will can't get to him because of the Genovesian so you are sitting on end seeing if Halt is dead or just injured. That is why I gave this book a five star. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6672706769155052855">Halt, Horace and Will are on the trail of Tennyson & his followers. The false prophet of the Outsider cult escaped justice for his crimes in Clonmel, & Halt is determined to stop him before he crosses the border into Araluen. Will has defeated one of Tennyson's Genovesan assassins in Clonmel -but there are two left alive. Are the extraordinary archery skills of Will and Halt enough to save them during a duel with the Genovesans . . . or is Will's mentor facing his last battle?(less)<br/><br/>Halt's Peril </span>
  <span id="freeText6672706769155052855" style="display:none">Halt, Horace and Will are on the trail of Tennyson &amp; his followers. The false prophet of the Outsider cult escaped justice for his crimes in Clonmel, &amp; Halt is determined to stop him before he crosses the border into Araluen. Will has defeated one of Tennyson's Genovesan assassins in Clonmel -but there are two left alive. Are the extraordinary archery skills of Will and Halt enough to save them during a duel with the Genovesans . . . or is Will's mentor facing his last battle?(less)<br /><br />Halt's Peril (Ranger's Apprentice #9) by John Flanagan continues the action of The Kings of Clonmel as Halt, Will &amp; Horace race to catch Tennyson &amp; his band. This is mostly straight forward action and suspense, with some very tension filled, emotional moments. There is the usual humor and male bonding interspursed, and we discover a bit more about how Halt feels about Will &amp; Horace. This is a bit slow at times and there's a bit more repitition than I prefer, but generally it's another satisfying adventure. Meeting Malcolm again is always a pleasure, as is encountering Shadow (Blackie). We see Halt feeling his age a little, and you wonder how soon this threesome may be broken up. I'm definitely looking forward to the next installment! For readers 10 and up.</span>

  <span id="freeText15978462411771805637" style="display:none">The Ranger's Apprentice series has been one of my favorites as I've watched the characters develop and when it arrived in at school on Friday, I grabbed it for my weekend read. While Halt's Peril was a good read, I feel that book 8, The Kings of Clonmel and Halt's Peril could have been combined into one tighter story. Readers already know that Rangers are skilled at concealment and very intelligent, that Horace is a dependable friend and knight. 150 pages passed before the plot advanced. Still worth reading though. I'll have to pass it on to others interested in the series and see what they think.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3379953-rusty?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3379953-rusty?shelf=children-ya">children-ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687999679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5139495580919543269">This is a delightful series and even though this is the ninth book I still enjoyed it very much. The characters are strong, funny at times, loyal to their friends and always brave but rarely foolhardy. In this episode Halt is injured when an enemy shoots a crossbow at him. Even though it appears to be only a scratch the injury fails to heal, becomes infected and Halt's personality begins to change. He becomes confused, collapses, sleeps a great deal and often raves when he is awake. He appears t</span>
  <span id="freeText5139495580919543269" style="display:none">This is a delightful series and even though this is the ninth book I still enjoyed it very much. The characters are strong, funny at times, loyal to their friends and always brave but rarely foolhardy. In this episode Halt is injured when an enemy shoots a crossbow at him. Even though it appears to be only a scratch the injury fails to heal, becomes infected and Halt's personality begins to change. He becomes confused, collapses, sleeps a great deal and often raves when he is awake. He appears to get better but suffers relapses. It is soon obvious that the crossbow bolt was poisoned. Young Will is devastated, cannot sleep, and sits by his mentor caring for him. The title indicates the theme of this tale. Can Halt recover? It appears unlikely as his condition gets increasingly worse. Readers will have to check this story out for themselves. The plot was different from other books in the series but so very well done that I recommend reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5139495580919543269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3141412085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2577857602435721337">This picks up right where Kings of Clonmel left off, with our favorite three adventurers in pursuit of Tennyson. <br/>It was much more rooted in suspense than it was adventure. Most of the time was spent tracking Tennyson or dealing with poisoning of Halt. <br/><br/>The resident Sorcerer of the North makes an appearance and he's a great addition to the trio, adding a mystical intelligence aspect alongside our cunning rangers and unbeatable warrior.<br/><br/>I enjoyed how the team finally took down Tennyson. I'm just not</span>
  <span id="freeText2577857602435721337" style="display:none">This picks up right where Kings of Clonmel left off, with our favorite three adventurers in pursuit of Tennyson. <br />It was much more rooted in suspense than it was adventure. Most of the time was spent tracking Tennyson or dealing with poisoning of Halt. <br /><br />The resident Sorcerer of the North makes an appearance and he's a great addition to the trio, adding a mystical intelligence aspect alongside our cunning rangers and unbeatable warrior.<br /><br />I enjoyed how the team finally took down Tennyson. I'm just not sure where the next in the series will go! There's only a few left, so I'm not sure how it will end </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2001052829?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lila Kims" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lila Kims" href="/user/show/67812854-lila-kims">Lila Kims</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001052829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11062779582350738059">Another enjoyable installment to the Ranger's Apprentice!! It moved slow at times, and I have my peeves with Flanagan's writing style, but this was a good book! The twist on Halt shocked me (in a good way!), bringing Malcolm back into the picture was a lot of fun, and Will's gift at the end was so sweet. The climax blew me away, as always, and the wrap-up ending... ALL THE FEELS.<br/><br/>However, two people I know told me that books 10 and 11 are boring. What do you guys say to that?</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZclwlbJjhOu5Rt13sCrIxubQTi9ye5SMaElUQpWoeWa1HAZMMz88VuLI8VzD8Nx72YUWkefQl8pXREnlhgAFxg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qsesDlCsrGiC17A4lY6FH9Hyf5WfepR1CkKBBSVExTd6EtrX0fAU1dlZnBPmVJGi7qcnKwrRlzM1T5yiNuy5lw==')})
  }

It wasn't until he wrote a highly uncomplimentary poem about a senior executive at the agency where he worked, however, that his talent was revealed. It turned out one of the company directors agreed with John's assessment of the executive, and happily agreed to train John in copywriting. <br /><br />After writing advertising copy for the next two decades, John teamed with an old friend to develop a television sitcom, Hey Dad!, which went on to air for eight years. <br /><br />John began writing Ranger's Apprentice for his son, Michael, ten years ago, and is still hard at work on the series. <br /><br />He currently lives in a suburb of Manly, Australia, with his wife. In addition to their son, they have two grown daughters and four grandsons.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/6534539-halt-s-peril">Quotes from Halt&#39;s Peril</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Does it matter?" Halt asked.<br /> Horace shrugged. "Not really, I suppose. I just wondered why you'd gone to the kitchen and why you took the trouble to remain unseen. Were you hiding from Master Chubb yourself? And Will just turned up by coincidence?"<br /> "And why would I be hiding from Master Chubb in his own kitchen?" Halt challenged. Again. Horace shrugged innocently.<br /> "Well,there was a tray of freshly made pies airing on the windowsill, wasn't there? And you're quite fond of pies, aren't you, Halt?" <br /> Halt drew himself up very straight in the saddle. "Are you accusing me of sneaking into that kitchen to steal the pies for myself? Is that it?"<br /> His voice and body language simply reeked of injured dignity.<br /> "Of course not, Halt!" Horace hurried to assure him, and Halt's stiff-shouldered form relaxed a little.<br /> "I just thought I'd give you the opportunity to confess," Horace added. This time, Malcolm couldn't conceal his sudden explosion of laughter. Halt gave them both a withering glance.<br /> "You know, Horace," he said at length, "you used to be a most agreeable young man. Whatever happened to you?"<br /> Horace turned a wide grin on him. "I've spent too much time around you, I suppose," he said.<br /> And Halt had to admit that was probably true.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/343873-does-it-matter-halt-asked-horace-shrugged-not-really-i">196 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Halt regarded him. He loved Horace like a younger brother. Even like a second son, after Will. He admired his skill with a sword and his courage in battle. But sometimes, just sometimes, he felt an overwhelming desire to ram the young warrior's head against a convenient tree.<br />"You have no sense of drama or symbolism, do you?" he asked.<br />"Huh?" replied Horace, not quite understanding. Halt looked around for a convenient tree. Luckily for Horace, there were none in sight.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/305230-halt-regarded-him-he-loved-horace-like-a-younger-brother">181 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
